## 05 Creating Polygonal Models
### 05-01 - Creating polygonal objects

Now let's start modeling in Maya
Typically in Maya
we model using what are called polygonal objects
And when we model with polygons
we typically start with a basic primitive and then shape that into the object that we want
So let's start off by creating some polygon primitives
Now we can do this in one of two places
We can go into the Create menu
and you'll see we have a lot of options here
but we want to find polygon primitives
Now I'm going to go here and just click on that dotted line at the top and tear this off
And you'll see that we have a number of different polygonal objects that we can create
Now there's another place you can find these as well
and that's on the shelf
So if you click on the Poly modeling shelf
you'll see we also have a number of these same primitives
So you can access these a little bit more easily here
But from the menu
you actually have a little bit more control
If I go down to the bottom of this menu
you'll see a little checkbox that says interactive creation
We can check this on
but for right now I'm going to check it off
And then we go
we'll go ahead and show you how that works
So let's go ahead up to the sphere
Now you'll notice that each one of these objects has a little box to the right and that controls the options for that particular object
So if I click on the one for the sphere
you'll see we have our polygon sphere options
which is the radius of the sphere
how many divisions
and how the object is oriented
So if I wanted to say
make my radius
say four
and hit create
it creates a sphere of radius 4 at the origin
And that's because I turned interactive creation off
It basically just took those values and place them at the origin of the scene
Now
if I turn on interactive creation and select sphere
I can left click and drag to make that sphere any size I want
Now
the sphere itself is controlled by what's called a node
Now we can find this in one of two places
If I go to the Attribute Editor
you'll see​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ here we have what's called polysphere 2
and this is the creation node
This is basically the same thing you have in that options box
so you can always come back to this and change the size of your sphere
So if I wanted to
I could type in 4 and make it exactly the same size as the other sphere
Now if I click on this sphere here
you'll see that it also has that same node
Now I can also find this in the channel box
so if I go to the channel box below all the translation values
you'll see I have this polysphere input
and that gives me all those same values as well
So I can certainly type in my number here
Now
this is the same for really any polygonal object
They will have their own nodes once you create them
Now I'm going to go ahead and select these spheres and delete them
And let's just take a look at some of the other polygonal primitives and see how they're creative
Now I'm going to leave interactive creation on and just select Cube
Now cube
you basically left click and drag and you drag out the base of the cube
It's really more of a box
it didn't have to be a cube
And then you left click again to raise it up
Now that polygon cube can have subdivisions for width
heightand depth
So again
for the cube
you can basically just left click and drag and then left click again to make that
I'm going to go ahead and delete these
the cylinder is very similar to the cube
you basically left click and drag out a base
Left click and drag the height cone
Againvery similar
but it has a pointy top
And then the torus is another really interesting one
And so what you have to do is you basically drag out the initial radius of it
and then the second click is that thickness of that doughnut or the torus
Now all of these really do have their own ways of creation
and it's always fun to just play with them and see how they're created
Nowif you want to
you can always click on the options box for these
And so you can kind of see how any one of these are built
And it just makes sense to explore these just to see what types of objects you can create in Maya
But just remember that polygonal objects are really the basis of everything that we build in Maya
And usually
you're going to start with a polygonal primitive when modeling


### 05-02 - Selecting polygonal components

When we model in Maya
we're basically just reshaping an object
We're moving parts of that object around to get the shape that we want
Nowthose parts are called components
and those are basically faces
edgesand vertices
Let me show you what I mean
So I'm going to go ahead and select this object and right click above it
And you'll see we get what's called the marking menu
Now it's got a lot of stuff in it
but I'm really just interested in vertex
edge and face
I'm going to go ahead and select vertices
and there we go
So these are basically the vertices that make up this object
Now they're basically just points
and I can select any one of those by right clicking on them
If I right click over the model again
I can move up to edge and select those
And those are essentially lines
So they're the lines that connect the vertices
If I right click again
I can select faces
and those faces are basically bordered by edges
So vertice​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌s are points
edges are lines
faces are 3D faces or planes
And so I'm going to go ahead and right click and select Vertex
Now
selecting vertices is pretty simple
All I have to do is left click on it
If I want to
I can hold down the Shift key and select multiple ones
or I can zoom out here and left click and drag to Marquee Select
Now
another way you can select is by using the greater than and less than keys on the keyboard
So if I hold down Shift and do greater than
you'll see that I'm expanding my selection
If I hit less than
it means I'm contracting my selection
Now another way to select is to select what are called basically edge loops or rings
So if I select a vertex and hold down the shift key and double click on an adjacent vertex
you'll see I get the entire ring
And I can do that in the other direction as well
And you'll see I'm getting something along this axis
And another way to select is if you select 1 vertex and basically go to something that's not adjacent but on the same line
and you can double click and select everything in between
Now let's take a look at edges
These are a little bit different
so I'm going to go ahead and right click
find my marking menu and select edge
and let's go ahead and we can again select edges
we can marquee select edges
Wellone of the nice things about edges is that they often form loops on your object
That can be really handy for reshaping that object
So if I hover over one edge and double click on it
it will select all adjacent edges
And so this is what's called all the edge loop
And if I want to
I can move that around or scale it to reshape my object
Nowif I double click on this one
it will go ahead and select along that axis as well
Now
just like with vertices
if I use greater than or less than
I can expand my selection as well
Now let's take a look at faces
So again I'm going to right click
find the marking menu and select face
And again
we can select faces individually or if I shift double click next to 1
I can select a ring of faces
So again
select this face and double click on the adjacent face and I'm selecting that
And just like with vertices
you can click on a face and then double click on something a little bit further away and you'll get all the faces in between
Nowone more little trick is if you just double click on a face
it will select all the connected faces of that object
And so you can basically select the whole model
So as you can see
there's a number of different ways to manipulate the shape of a model using vertices
edgesand faces
and there's also a number of different ways to select these components


### 05-03 - Using the Modeling Toolkit

Maya's modeling toolkit has a number of features that will help you model faster
So let's take a look at how to use some of the basics
I'm going to select this spinner
which is the front of that propeller
and let's go up here
And on the top left
you'll see this button with a little hammer on it
And I'm going to select it
and that's the Modeling Toolkit
Now this will show up as a tab
so you can also press that tab
Now
the first thing about the Modeling Toolkit is that it allows you to select vertices
edgesand faces without going to a marking menu
So here I can select vertices
here I can select edges and faces
So that's one way to use this
You can also go back into object mode
Now
another really nice feature is symmetry
So if I select vertices
let's go ahead and select some of the vertices around this opening
So right there
now we have symmetry
and this allows you to model objects symmetrically
Now we can do that around the object's own pivot
So if you have that pivot centered
it will go ahead and mirror around that centered pivot
Or we can use the world axes
And that means that the object has to be centered to the world
So I'm going to select object X
and when I do
notice how the other side lights up
So if I select vertices on this side
it selects the corresponding vertices on the other side
So if I were to
sayselect these ones
I could maybe move those vertices to maybe close that up
Or if I wanted to
I could select basically all of these and then maybe scale them down to close that opening up if I wanted to
Now
another really nice feature is called Soft Select
So I'm going to go ahead and turn off symmetry and let's go ahead and select this nacelle
And I'm going to go back into vertex mode
And let's go ahead and select these vertices at the end of that leg
Nowif you scroll down a little bit
you'll see we have soft selection
All I have to do is switch that on and you'll notice a change
And that basically allows me to fall off those vertices
So with it off
if I move these vertices
you'll see I get this effect
If I turn on soft select
and right now my value is at 2
I will get a much more organic modeling ​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌effect
Then you can instantly see how this can help your modeling
Nowif I want to
I can make that fall off smaller
So let's say I make it one
We can basically have a smaller fall off or a larger one
Let's say I make it three
that will get almost the entire leg
Now we can fall off by surface or volume
Nowif I fall off by surface
that means it will measure the distance from the vertices along the surface
If you fall off by volume
that means it will measure in 3D space from those vertices
So in this case
if I do it by volume
you'll see it's affecting that other leg
And if I do it by surface
then it's only affecting this leg
So you have to be aware of this pull down
When you work with sauce selection
typically I keep it on surface
Nowin addition to this
you can also change the shape of this curve to control the fall-off even more precisely
Now
the Modeling Toolkit also has a whole bunch of other tools down here
Now we're going to go over a lot of these
and they're actually mirrored in the modeling interface here
So if I select my Modeling menu set
you'll see a lot of these are in those menus use as well
So this is just
againanother way to get to these tools a little bit more quickly than digging through menus
But I find that the Modeling Toolkit is really handy
particularly for symmetry and soft selects
So go ahead and play with those and get used to using symmetry and soft Select in your modeling


### 05-04 - Component tags

Maya's component tags help you remember the selections of your components when modeling in Maya
So let's take a look at this
I'm going to select this engine pod and hop over to the Attribute Editor
Now in the Attribute Editor
we have a couple of different tabs here
and the first tab is the main node
and that contains all of your translation information
The second tab should be the shape node
and that contains the geometry information for the object
So in this shape node
you should have a roll-out called component tags
So if I click on that and scroll down
you'll see I have a couple of component tags already set up
So before we use these
let me explain how this works
We have our component tag name
so basically just a descriptive name
We have the type of components
so faces
verticesand edges
the location
in other words
what object we're using that on
as well as some numbers for how many of those objects are selected
So if I highlight body faces and right click over it
you can select those components
And so basically
those are the faces that comprise the body of the object
If I right click over strut A I'll select those
those are vertices that comprise that strut
This one here is just the tip of that strut and its edges
So hopefully you can see how handy this will be when selecting difficult parts of a model
You know
if you have something that's really hard to select
once you get it
you kind of want to put a tag on it just so you can get back to it if needed
Now let's go ahead and show you how to create your own component tag
So I'm going to go ahead and right click over my object
going to vertex mode
And let's go ahead and select these vertices
And then I'm going to expand this selection by hitting the greater than sign a couple of times
So let's go ahead and go out to maybe there
Now once I have my selection and I want to save it as a tag
all I have​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ ### 05-05 - Using brush tools to sculpt meshes

If you want to model organically in Maya
you can use the sculpting tools
Nowthe sculpting tools can be found in a couple of different places
We do have a sculpting shelf here
And also if you're in the modeling menu set
you can go into mesh tools
sculpting tools
Now I'm going to go ahead and tear this off
You can see it's a very big menu here
And before we do anything I'm actually going to go ahead and turn off these textures so that we can see our sculpt a little bit easier
So I'm going to go ahead and just switch off hardware texturing by clicking on that checkered sphere and let's go ahead and turn on Wireframe on Shaded
That way we can see as we sculpt
So to get to the Sculpt tool
all you have to do is go into the menu or the shelf and select it
Now I'm going to go ahead and select the options here by going to this box here on the right
Now what this does is it brings up our sculpting tools
Now if I click on an object here I'm going to go ahead and click on this plane
You'll see that we get this round cursor
which is our brush
Now we can affect that size simply by adjusting it here in the tool settings
or if you hold down the letter B and left click and drag
you can make that bigger or smaller
Nowin addition to brush size
we also have strength
So I'm going to go ahead and turn that down to maybe about 6 or 7 or so
and then just left click and drag
And as you can see I'm now sculpting this mesh
So the more I click over the same area
the more it sculpts it up And as you can see
I can basically reshape this however I want
Now
the sculpt tool is just one of many tools that you can use
We have a whole bunch of different tools
probably the most important of which is the smooth tool
and this will allow you to smooth out your mesh
So I'm going to go ahead and go over this
and I'm going to turn my strength down to maybe about 50% here
and then maybe make my brush a little bit bigger
So I'm going to
againhold down the letter B
left click and drag
And as you can see
this smooths it out
Now
in addition to the brush tool
you can also do a flood
And so what it will do is it will flood the entire object at this particular str​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ you can see that I can only affect those parts of the mesh that have a vertex
So if I were to basically brush here
nothing happens
If I brush over a vertex
then it will change
So go to right click and hit Exit Sculpting and let's suck and again
go to the Sculpt tool
Now in this one
you'll see that
wellI have a lot more vertices
so that gives me a lot more places to sculpt
And so this allows me to have a lot more fine control simply because I have more details
So if I wanted to say maybe smooth this a bit
I could do that
And again
because I have more detail
I can get a better or basically more detailed sculpt
So this is kind of a balance
You will want enough detail so that you can sculpt
but not so much that it weighs the model down
And again
I can right click and do exit sculpting
So as you can see
the sculpt tools in Maya give you a really great way to organically sculpt


## 06 Modeling Polygonal Meshes
### 06-01 - Setting up reference

Many times when we model
we'll be modeling against a reference image
And in Maya
we can set this up fairly easily
Nowin this scene
I already have some images set up
So if we hop over to the channel box and go down to layers
you'll see we have this layer called reference
So if I click here and make those layers visible
you'll see that we have a couple of image planes for that blimp that we were working with previously
So if I wanted to model a blimp
I could use this to get the shape exactly the way that I want
So let's take a look at how to set this up
So I'm going to go ahead and hit the letter V and hide that
And let's go ahead and zoom in a little bit
So what I want to do is create a piece of geometry
and then I'm going to map those images onto it
So let's take a look at the images we're using
So I'm here in Photoshop
and you'll see I have a front and a side view of that blimp
Nowone of the things you'll know is that both of these images are the same size and aspect ratio
I've actually made them square because that don't just make it a lot easier to map them onto geometry
And even though the blimp is kind of long and skinny I'm still putting it on a square image
I've also added some light red guidelines just so I can line things up once I'm in Maya
So now that we're in Maya
all we have to do is create a piece of geometry
And so I'm just going to create a plane and then map those images onto it
So what I want to do is I want to go into create polygon primitives
And I'm going to turn off interactive creation
And then I'm going to create a plane
And I'm going to go over here and click on the options for that plane
So what I want to do is create a plane with the same width and height
So I'm going to make the width 10
the height 10
and then I want to make sure that I just dial those divisions down to one in each direction
And I also want to make sure that create U V's is checked
And that will make sure that my mapping lines up
So when I do that and hit create
it creates a 10 by 10 plane
And so I can move that up so I can see it a little bit better
And now all we have to do is map the image onto that
So the easiest way to do that is to just hop over to the rendering shelf
Now we're going to start working with materials here
and I'm just going to give you a little taste of it
We're going to dive into it much deeper a little bit later in the course
But what we're going to do is we're going going to apply a material to it and then add a bitmap to that material
So here on the rendering shelf I'm going to look for the one without the highlight
and that should be a Lambert material
If I keep my plane selected
all I have to do is left click on this button and it applies that material
And now all I have to do is go over to my Attribute Editor and you'll see on the far right hand side
I have this tab called Lambert 7
And that's basically the material I just applied
So if I go down here to common material attributes
you'll see ### 06-03 - Using the Extrude tools

When we model
we may need to add additional detail to our primitives
And one of the easiest ways to do this is to use what's called the Extrude tool
So I've got this engine pod here
and let's go ahead and use Extrude
So typically we use Extrude on faces
so I'm going to select some faces here
So I'm going to right click in my marketing menu
select face
and then I'm going to shift select these faces here
So I've got about eight faces selected
and then we can do our extrude from a couple of places
If we're in the modeling menu set
we can go to edit mesh
extrude the hockey for that is control E
if you're in the Modeling toolkit
we also have an Extrude as well
But typically I like to use the hot key
so I'm going to hit Control E
and that starts my extrude
Now what I get here is I get this gizmo that allows me to control the extrude as well
well as this dialog box that controls it as well
So I can use either one
So all I have to do is select this blue arrow and push it out or in
So if I bring it out
you'll see that local translate is affected in that dialogue box
Now I also have a thickness
which basically does the same thing
so typically I just use local translate
we also have offset
which basically scales it
We can add more divisions if we want
And then we also have what's called keep faces together
So right now it's on and my faces are together
If I left click on this
it turns off and you'll see I get this kind of spiky look
Now typically we don't want that
so I'm going to left click on it again and keep those together
And then all we have to do is position this where we want
We can use the scale tools to scale it up
dow​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ we want
And when we're done
all we have to do is left click off of it
and now my extrude is complete
Now I can continue to do that
If I wanted to
I could say select these faces here and again
hit control E
bring them up
and maybe just scale them down quite a bit
something like that

And then maybe do the same thing for this
Now I've got these selected
I can basically extrude these
do the same thing
maybe just bring that offset down
maybe scale it down just a little bit
And there we go
Now one of the nice things about Extrude is that you can extrude multiple sets of faces at once
So if I were to say select
select the tops of this and maybe the tops of that
and then hit control E to extrude
I can extrude these in parallel
And then again
I can just play with my offset and I can make parallel legs that are basically the same same length basically
and I can start working from there
So as you can see
extrude is a great way to add additional detail to your models


### 06-04 - Working with edge loops

When you work with polygonal models
you'll often be working with what are called edge loops
And those are basically just loops of edges that define the outline of the model
And it's a great way to quickly change the loop and feel of your model
So let's go ahead and select the back part of this engine pod here
And so if I want to
I can right click and go into edge mode here and I can select edges
Now we've seen if you double click on an edge
it'll select that loop
And that's basically all an edge loop is
It's just a loop of edges that connect together
So if I don't click here
you'll see I have an edge loop that goes vertically and this one goes horizontally
And as you can see
these edge loops basically define the outline of this
So if I double clicked here and maybe scaled that down or scaled it up
you can see how I can change the outline of it
Now if I double clicked and shift double clicked on the second one
you can see I can again make a bulge or I can kind of make a waste on that if I want
Now these legs also can be modified
Now one of the nice things about edge​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ loops is that you can add additional edge loops if you need more detail
So we can do that under mesh tools
We have a couple of tools now
The most important one is insert edge loops
So I'm going to go ahead and select that
and then I'm going to click on one of these lengthwise edges
And you'll see that when I do that
it creates an edge loop that runs perpendicular to that
So if I do that
it creates an edge loop in the middle
I can do the same up here and create one here
Nowonce I have that edge loop
I can
for example
scale it to narrow it or scale it up to make it a little bit fatter
And as you can see
is a very easy way to control the shape of that object
Now
there are other tools that allow you to work with edge loops as well
So if we go into mesh tools
I also have what's called offset edge loop
And if I click on an edge loop here
it will basically create bounding edges as well
So I can create edges that basically surround 1 edge loop
So now I have all of these and that gives me more detail to shape that particular part of the model
Now
another nice thing about edge loops is that it will allow you to move them
So we have under mesh tools
we have what's called slide edge
So if I select that double click to select that loop
I can then middle click
And that will slide the edge
So I double click to select the loop
middle click to slide it
Now I can do this for single edges as well
So if I selected this edge and middle clicked
I could slide that
Now one of the nice things about slide edge is that it preserves the outline of the model
So if I double click here and middle click and drag
you'll see that that edge loop is actually getting bigger as it goes towards this direction
or smaller as it goes towards this direction
So it's a great way to add detail exactly where you want
and then you can sculpt from there
So when you work with polygonal models
be sure to use edge loops to define the shape of the model as well as to add and arrange the detail of your models


### 06-05 - Combine and Separate

When we model objects
sometimes we'll get multiple surfaces
and sometimes you'll want to combine those surfaces so you have a single object
And we can do this in may-a using combine and separate for polygonal objects
So let's take a look at this
So I've got this blimp
and you can see this blimp is all sorts of different objects
So I've got the blimp body
I've got different objects for the tail
that little dock in the front
as well as the gondola and the windows
Now
let's say I wanted to simplify this a little bit
so I'm going to go ahead and just marquee select the gondola and the windows
and then if I'm in my modeling menu set
I can go over to mesh combine
And when I do that
watch what happens
The original gondola and windows kind of go away
they become references
and then I've got this other object here
and that's called Windows because that was the last object I selected
and now that's just one object
So if I right click go into vertex mode
I can actually model this
And you can see that this whole object is basically appears as one object
If I right clicked and went on
sayface mode
you could see one of the things about this is that the faces are not connected
So if I were to say
you know
pull out one of these windows here
you could see that that geometry is not connected to the gondola
So the windows and gondola are still not connected
but they're part of that same geometry
Now
I could go through some additional processes to connect everything up
And this combined would be the first part of that
So I'm going Na
go ahead and go back into object mode
and we also have an operation called separate
which basically breaks things apart
So let's go ahead and select the blimp and all of the tails here
So I'm going to select blimp and ​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ this time it's called blimp
So now when I select this

If I was right after when I combined them

Now I have this surface here
which is the blimp
and then the other four are the tail surfaces
So you can combine polygonal objects into one object or you can separate objects as well
and that will separate out all the unconnected parts of that polygonal object


### 06-06 - Object History

As you model in Maya Maya keeps track of everything that you do
It creates a history of all of your operations
Now we can manage this history in Maya
So let's go ahead and select this blimp
Now this blimp was combined and I did a couple of other options to it
and if we look in the Attribute Editor
those all show up in the nodes
So we have our basic blimp
We also have our shape node
which is always there
But then as we start to work on this model
you'll see that we get additional nodes
So the more stuff you do
the more nodes you have
and this can get really complex and can start to bog down the scene a little bit
So we can clean this up by deleting what's called history
We can go into edit
delete by type history
Now we can do one of two operations
we can delete by type for the specific object
or we can delete all by type for the entire scene and again
the top option for each of these is history

is my blimp
my shape node
and then the material nodes
So we can do that again for this gondola here
So you see that we have Gondola one

delete by type history
and now that has simplified as well

but if you have a really complex scene
it's a great way just to kind of clean up the scene and kind of give everything a fresh start
So as you work Maya creates a history of your operations
And there's a point where you'll need to clean this up
And you do that by deleting history


## 07 Additional Modeling Techniques
### 07-01 - Object deformers

Another way to change the shape of your models is to use the formers
Now these can be used for animation or modeling
So we're going to take a look at modeling with the former
So here I am in my modeling menu set
and you'll see we have a deformed menu
Now this is a pretty big menu with lots of stuff on it
So let's go ahead and just look at a few of these and kind of get the idea as to how they work
So I'm going to select my blimp here and under deform I'm going to go to Lattice
and then I'm going to select the options for that
Now for the settings I'm going to plug in 4
4and 4 for the divisions and then hit create
Now what this does is it creates a box around my object or whatever I have selected
and I can then deform that box to deform whatever's inside of it
So you'll see here that it's created what's ca​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ FFT base and an FFT lattice
So what we want to do is make sure that that lattice is selected
and then we can right click to get a marking menu
And what we're going to do is look at lattice points

So all I have to do is select these just like I would vertices
and I can move

So really whatever you want
Now
if you want to get rid of this deformation
you can just right click

and just hit delete
And then it goes away and the deformation goes away with it
Now you can also deform parts of an object
so all you have to do is select some components and then deform those

go into Vertex
and I'm just going to select the vertices along the front of this blimp and then just go back into deform lattice
And it's remembered that 4 by 4 lattice
and so there we go
So now again
I can deform that portion of the model
So if I go into lattice point
by right clicking

So now I'm only deforming just a small section of the model
Now again
I can right click and go back in the object mode to get the lattice itself
Nowif you want to bake this in

but there's always the chance that this lattice will move and affect the model
So typically

So I'm going to go ahead and select my blib edit
delete by type history
Now that deletes the lattice and bakes in the deformation
Now
there's a lot of other types of deformers that

So we go into deform

So I'm going to tear this off so we can see them
And you'll see we have about six of them
So let's look at a couple of these
Now I'm not going to do this on the blimp
so I'm going to go over to my channel box and go down to my layers menu
I'm going to turn off the blimp layer and turn on the props layer and let's go ahead and zoom in
So if I select this prop
I can deform it
So let's take a look at the bend deformer
So I'm just going to go ahead and click on that and apply it
And you'll see what happens is that I get this bend handle in my scene and that that's applied to my prop
Nowif I have that bend handle selected
I can go over to the Attribute Editor and you'll see we have a number of options here
So we have curvature
and we have low and high bound and so on
But this is actually going vertically
and it's bending along that y axis
So I kind of want to rotate that into something a little bit more in line with that propeller
So I'm going to rotate it this way here along the z or Z axis
And so let's just rotate it 90 degrees along Z
and now let's go ahead and select that bend handle
Go into the Attribute Editor
let's find that bend one node
So now the curvature
so you can see I can curve the whole thing
or I can create what's called a low and a high bound
So let's go ahead and curve it up like this
And so my high bound is on this side
And so if I dial that down
that means that it's only going to affect this portion of it
So again
I can affect that low bound to affect only part of that model
Nowjust like with the lattice
if I don't want this to deform
I can just select the handle and hit the lead
Now another one that's probably a little more practical for this propeller is twist
So here I have this propeller
If you take a look at it
it's pretty straight
so propellers actually do twist a bit
so let's use the twist modifier
So I'm going Na
select that propeller
hit twist
and again
it comes in at this orientation
So let's go ahead and rotate it
In the channel box
We're going to rotate it
say 90 degrees
and then I'm going to keep that twist handle selected
go to the Attribute Editor
and then you can see we have a start angle
an end angle
Now I don't need an end angle because it needs to be straight on this side
And then we also have a low bound and a high bound
So I'm going dial that high bound up so that this kind of axle part of the propeller isn't twisted
So we're just twisting the part with the wing on it
And so then I'm going to twist it
maybe say negative 60
and there we go
And so that's very easily I've turned that straight piece of geometry into something that resembles a propeller
So these deformers can be very handy for creating these types of shapes
And there's a lot of other deformers that Maya has
and I would encourage you to explore them and use them in your work


### 07-02 - Mirroring and merging components

There are many times when we'll need to model or create symmetrical objects
and one way to do this is to model one side of the object and then just mirror it to create the other side
So let's take a look at how to do that
So here I have a propeller
and I want to create the other side
And I want to attach it all as one propeller assembly
Well
the first thing you want to do is you want to make sure that you have everything lined up so that you can mirror it
So in this case I've got this propeller and if I hit W to move
you'll see that the pivot point is kind of in the middle of that propeller
So I need to get it towards the center
So I'm just going to tap my space bar
hop out to a fore view and find my front view
So I'm going to tap again and then all I have to do is hold down the letter D and that allows me to move my pivot And I'm just going to center that to that propeller assembly
And also I'm centering it to the world
Wellso everything in this scene is pretty much centered
So now once I have that
I now have a pivot point that is centered to my object
so that will rotate around the center and it will also mirror around that center
So let's go ahead and select this propeller and mirror it
Now we can do this in a couple of ways
TypicallyI just do it manually
I duplicate it
and then I flip it
But you could actually go into edit
duplicate special
and set up a negative scale and make it just one copy
and that would do the same thing
But let's go ahead and do it manually
So you see the process
So I'm going to keep my Prop 0 1 selected and just hit Control D
and that makes a copy
it duplicates it
And so now I have Prop 0 1 and Prop 0 2
and they're in exactly the same place
So I'm going to take Prop O2
and let's just scale it negative one in x
and that flips it around that way
But you'll see the leading edge of this propeller is on the same side as this other one
And I want this flip vertically
so my vertical axis is Y
and I'm just going to go a negative one for scale and y
so now I have my object mirrored the way that I want
Now I need to attach everything
So let's go ahead and just select these two objects here
and I'm going to hit control H to hide them
So what we want to do is we want to attach this propeller to this propeller
Wellyou'll notice that they're kind of a little out of alignment here
so I'm going to hit my space bar and let's go into a side view and let's turn on wireframe mode
And so what I want to do is I'm just going to move this one up so that you can see in Wireframe view that this top edge
I just want those all to along
Nowonce I have that
they're pretty much aligned and now I can connect or basically bridge this gap
Now
the way we do that is the first thing we need to do is we need to make it one object
So we've done this before
All we need to do is do a mesh combined
So now both surfaces are technically one object here
So now I have this prop 3
which is both of these
and then I need to connect both sides
Now there's a couple of ways to do it
So I'm going to show you both
Now
both of these require that the ends of those propellers are open
so I'm going to right click
go into face mode
and then shift select these faces right on the end and hit delete
And you can see that opens it up
Do the same over here
So we want that basically to be open
We don't want to face covering that
And now I can basically bridge this gap
Now the manual way to do this is to do what's called a weld
so I can just right click on this select vertex
and then under Mesh tools
I have what's called Target weld
So I can do this for either vertices or edges
So we're going to do it with vertices
So if I select Target Weld
I can hover over any one of these vertices
left click
and drag to another vertex
and once that snaps
let go and it's welded
So basically I'm just connecting all of these manually
Now this is not really the way that I want to do this
So let's go ahead and undo our way out of this
And I'll show you the other way
So this way requires that we select the open edges
So I'm going to right click
go into edge mode and basically select these edges
So I'm going to go ahead and shift
select my way all the way around
So each one of these get selected and then the same on the opposite side
So I want to make sure I have both of those selected
And once I do
there's a command under edit mesh called Bridge
And there we go
it just bridges the gap
Now I can add divisions if I want more detail in that gap
I can also add things such as taper and twist in case it doesn't align properly
But this seems to have gone pretty well
So I'm just going to go ahead and leave it as is and then click off of it
So now I have a propeller that is basically connected
and now that I have this additional detail here
I can add ​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ edge loops if I want and model it to create a propeller shaft or really whatever I want
But hopefully this gives you some insight into how to mirror and connect geometry to create symmetrical objects

we typically start off with a low resolution model
and then we add detail as needed
Now

So here I have a propeller
and I'm going to go ahead and select it
Let's turn on Wireframe on Shaded
And you can see that this propeller was modeled pretty low resolutions
So there's really not a lot of detail here
And so these edges are a little rough
So if we got close to this
this might be visible
you know
far away
maybe it's okay
but now not quite
So if we want to
we can add detail through smoothing
So I'm going Na

ahead and select this propeller and go mesh smooth
And when I do
it brings up this floating menu that is the number of divisions for the smoothie
Now when it subdivides and mesh
it basically just takes each face and cuts it into corners and then smooths that out

it cuts them again
So in other words
it goes 4 and then 16 and then 64
So it's really powers of 2
So you got to be a little bit careful about how many divisions you use
You can actually kind of blow things up if you go a little bit too high

and it's nice and smooth and that should render really nicely

our number of divisions

And then this part here is a little bit more squared off
So if you need to add detail and make your object a little bit smoother Maya smoothing tool is a great way to do it for your models


### 07-04 - Working with subdivision surfaces

A more efficient way to smooth objects is to use what are called subdivision surfaces
Nowthese smooth the object at render time
but leave the original low resolution geometry
And that way you can work with low res geometry without the additional weight of a smooth object
So if I were to take
sayfor example
this propeller and I would to go mesh smooth
and maybe I smoothed it twice
that's basically 16 times as much detail
And that's a lot of weight for that particular object
Now I'm going to go ahead and basically just undo that
And if we want to
we can actually use what are called subdivision surfaces
which will do the same thing but leave the original model
Now
this is basically just some keys on your keyboard
So if I hit one
that's basically the basic model
If I hit 2
this will smooth the object
but also leave the original model as what's called the cage
So here is my original model
and this is what it looks like when it's smooth
So again
onethe original model 2 is smooth
Now if I go to 3
that just deletes the cage and shows me the smooth object
And so visually
I get basically the same thing as a smoothed object without the additional weight of all those polygons
Because if I hit one
that's the object that I'm working with
but this is the object that I see
Now
this can also be used as a modeling tool
So I'm going to go ahead and hit two
And let's take a look at this
So if I right click and maybe go into edge mode here
I can maybe double click on this edge and select that edge loop
And if I move that edge loop
you can see how as it moves closer to the next edge
that curve gets tighter
And if I move it away
the curve gets broader
So this is one way to control the curvature of your smooth objects
So again
if I double click on this one
you can again see how that affects the underlying model
And then when I hit 3
you'll see that the model looks a little bit different
Now let's go a little bit further with this concept
I'm going Na
go ahead and select this object here
And let's go ahead and hit three to do a subdivision surface
Now what you see here is we're kind of getting this artifact here
and so maybe it's not smoothing exactly the way that we want
we want this curve to be a little bit sharper as it connects to that propeller
Wellagain
we can use edge loops to control that curvature
So actually I'm going to hit two here
and you'll see that this is what the cage is
And so what this is doing is that it's basically interpolating between this edge loop and this edge loop
so all I have to do is add a little bit more detail or move the existing details
So in this case I'm just going to do mesh tools
insert edge loop
and I'm going to insert an edge loop right very close to that next edge
And what this does is it creates a very sharp corner
Now if I l​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ that edge loop selected and do a slide edge
I can middle click and drag
and you can see how that curvature changes as it gets closer to the next edge
So subdivision surfaces can be a really fast way to smooth surfaces
They can also help you with modeling your objects so that they smooth better



### 07-05 - Boolean tools

One more way to model with polygons is to do what are called Booleans
Nowthis allows you to add
subtractand intersect multiple polygonal objects
So we can find Booleans under mesh Booleans
So let's go ahead and tear that off
And you'll see we have a number of operations here
and let's go through some of them
So I'm going to select this cylinder and just move it so that it's inside this box
Now with a Boolean
all I have to do is select both objects
I'm going to select the cube and the cylinder
and let's just do what's called a union
And what that does is it basically creates a third object
So you see I have my original cube and cylinder plus this poly surface 1
Now I'm going to move this a little bit off so you can kind of see how this works
So what it's done is it's basically created one object out of both surfaces
but I do have both of those surfaces that are live
Nowthis is going to be in effect until I do something like delete history
So with history active
I can actually select that original cylinder and move it around
And I can actually change that Boolean
Now I'm going to go ahead and undo my way out of this
So let's go ahead and get it to the point where that poly surface 1 goes away and let's take a look at some of the other ones
So we have difference a minus b and b minus a
so I'm going to go ahead and select my cylinder and then shift select my box
and let's do difference a minus b
so it's going to be cylinder minus box
and there we go
So the cylinder gets the box subtracted out of it
I'm going to go ahead and undo that
Let's subtract the cylinder from the box
So that's B minus a
and so that's a great way to get a hole in an object
So I'm going to go ahead and select that poly surface 1
and again
the surface is live
so if I move this cylinder
you can see the hole also moves with it
Nowyou may think that this is a great way to create holes in objects
And for this type of object
yesit might be a great way to do it
But as soon as you start to deform or smooth the object
you're going to get a problem
So let's just go ahead and hit the number 3 to subdivide this object
And you can see right now I'm getting all these jaggedy edges
And that's because things aren't really lining up
You're not getting a clean hole in that object
And that's why the smoothing really isn't working
So I'm going to go ahead and hit one and then again I'm just going to undo my way out of this
Now
the last one is intersection
and that's pretty self explanatory
So all it does is it basically shows you the part of the object that is common to both
Now I've been doing this with two objects
but you can do Booleans with free objects
basically unions and intersections
You can't do differences because those are only two opera ends
So let's say I take this sphere here
and I move it so that it's basically here
it's over all of these
So once I have that positioned
I just select all of them and do a union
And again
I can select that poly surface 1
And there we go
So now again
I can move that and affect it
And if you want to
you could also do this as an intersection
So I've undo my way out of this and hit intersection
and that's just that part​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ where all three of those overlaps
So typically
I use this with only two objects
but you can certainly use more than two if you want
and if that makes sense for your project
But remember
Booleans are really just more for mechanical type of objects
As soon as you get into deformations or subdivisions or smoothing
you may have problems
So just be careful when you use Booleans in Maya


## 08 Working with Curves
### 08-01 - Creating curves

Maya also has the ability to create curves
and these can be used for a number of different purposes
You can use them as modeling tools
animation tools
visual effects
and so on
So let's take a look at some basic ways to draw curves
Nowcurves can be found in a couple of places
In Maya
we do have a shelf
dedic​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​​​‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌​​​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌​​​‌‌​‌​‌​​‌‌‌‌​‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌​‌‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌‌‌‌‌​​‌‌​‌‌‌​​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​‌‌‌‌​‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​​‌‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌‌​​‌​​‌‌​‌​‌‌‌​‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌‌ated curves
and we have a lot of tools here that you can use
We also have it in the menu system
So if we're going to create
you'll see that they exist in two places under nerves
primitives
We have a circle and a square
which are curves
We also have Curves tools
which allows to create a bunch of other types of curves
So we're going to start off with a circle
So I'm going to go into nerves primitives
make sure interactive creation is turned on
and select circle
and then just left click and drag on the grid
And so here's my circle
Now this greats what's called a nerd curve
and we can modify this just like we can with polygonal objects
So I'm going to right click
and then you'll see we have a number of options or a number of components that we can use
Now in this case I'm going to select Control Vertex
Now this is very similar to a vertex on a polygonal object
but it controls the curve and you'll see we have a number of these control vertexes arrayed around the curve
So if I select one of those and move it
I can manipulate the shape of that curve
Now notice that two of these control vertices have a different shape
So here I have one that's square
and that means that it's the first vertex in the curve
Now curves in Maya have a direction
and that can be important when you get to certain types of operations
So the square tells you that that's the first vertex
Nowthe second type of vertex here is the one that's shaped like a u
and that's basically what tells you the direction
So that's the second vertex in the curve
So this is the first one
and this is the second one
And the rest of them are just dots
But this determines the direction of this curve
And in this case
it's going counterclockwise
So let's go ahead and just go back in object mode
and I'm going to go ahead and delete that circle
and let's create some other types of curves
So I'm going to go back into my Create menu and under Curve Tools I'm just going to tear that off
So we have it very handy
And let's start off with the c-v curve tool
Now CV means control vertex and let's go ahead and create one
So this is going to create a nerves curve
So when I lay down that first vertex by left clicking
you can see I get the square
The second vertex is the u
the 3rd vertex is a dot
And then the curve doesn't actually show up until I hit that fourth vertex
So you need a minimum of four points to determine a nerves curve
Nowonce I have those 4
I can just keep clicking and making the curve however I want
Nowonce I'm done
all I have to do is hit enter and that locks in the curve
Now if I right click on this
I can go back to those control vertices
select them
and manipulate the shape of the curve
Now
there are other ways to create curves
So let's take a look at the EP curve tool
Now
this is a different creation method for a nerves curve
So when I select this
notice how I lay down a dot
but it actually shows up a little bit differently
shows up kind of like a little cross or an X
and then the next one
notice how the curve is actually drawing between those
So I'm actually seeing the curve as I draw it
So this is really just a different input method
But once I hit enter
the curve shows up
And then when I go to edit it by right clicking and I go to control Vertex
notice how again I'm getting the Cv's of a nerves curve
So this is just a different way to input your curves and may be more accurate in certain situations so you can decide when to use it and when to go back to the c-v curve tool
So again I'm just going to move this over to the side
And now let's take a look at the Bezier curve tool
Nowthis is very similar to what we would see in say Adobe Illustrator
So instead of just clicking
you can click and drag
and that drags out what's called Bezier handle
And then I can use that to create basically the same topic curves you would see in Illustrator
Now I don't have to click and drag
If I just click
it creates right angles
which can be very handy in certain situations
And again
once I hit enter
that curve locks in
But if I right click and go into Control vertex
you'll see that all of these control vertices have the handle
so you can still manipulate those as Bezier curves
So this is a very different type of curve
And it can be very useful
particularly if you want to get things such as right angles or straight lines
And finally
we have what's called the pencil curve tool
Nowif I click on this
all I have to do is left click and drag
and it basically allows me to draw like a pencil
Once I let go
it turns that into a curve
and then I can right click above that curve
go into control vertex and notice how it basically creates a nerves curve again
but probably a little bit more finely detailed than what we had drawn previously
And that's because the curve that we drew was a little bit less specific because we used the pencil tool
So these are some ways to create and draw curves in Maya
And as you need curves
these will become very
very handy
